<p><b>Annika Sörenstam</b> (<small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Swedish" title="Help:IPA for Swedish">[ˈan.niː.ka ˌsøː.rɛn.ˈstam]</a></span>; <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Annika_S%C3%B6renstam.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Sv-Annika_S%C3%B6renstam.ogg" title="Sv-Annika Sörenstam.ogg">listen</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Annika_S%C3%B6renstam.ogg" title="File:Sv-Annika Sörenstam.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>; born 9 October 1970) is a retired Swedish <a href="/wiki/Professional_golfer" title="Professional golfer">professional golfer</a>, one of the most successful female golfers in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LPGA_Wins_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-LPGA_Wins-1">[1]</a></sup> Before stepping away from competitive golf at the end of the 2008 season, she had won 90 international tournaments as a professional, making her the female golfer with the most wins to her name. She has won 72 official <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">LPGA</a> tournaments including ten <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women%27s_majors" title="Women's majors">majors</a> and 18 other tournaments internationally, and she tops the LPGA's career money list with earnings of over $22 million—over $2 million ahead of <a href="/wiki/Karrie_Webb" title="Karrie Webb">her nearest rival</a> while playing 149 fewer events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Since 2006, Sörenstam has held dual American and Swedish citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizenship_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-citizenship-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The winner of a record eight <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour#LPGA_Tour_awards" title="LPGA Tour">Player of the Year</a> awards, and six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour#LPGA_Tour_awards" title="LPGA Tour">Vare Trophies</a> given to the LPGA player with the lowest seasonal scoring average, she is the only female golfer to shoot a 59 in competition. She holds various all-time scoring records including the lowest season scoring average: 68.6969 in 2004.</p>
<p>Representing Europe in the <a href="/wiki/Solheim_Cup" title="Solheim Cup">Solheim Cup</a> on eight occasions between 1994 and 2007, Sörenstam was the event's <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Solheim_Cup_golfers#Record_European_point_winners" title="List of European Solheim Cup golfers">all-time leading points earner</a> until her record was surpassed by England's <a href="/wiki/Laura_Davies" title="Laura Davies">Laura Davies</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2011_Solheim_Cup" title="2011 Solheim Cup">2011 Solheim Cup</a>.</p>
<p>In 2003, Sörenstam made history at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Colonial" title="Bank of America Colonial">Bank of America Colonial</a> tournament as the first woman to play in a <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a> event since 1945.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood_and_amateur_career">Childhood and amateur career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Childhood and amateur career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Bro,_Stockholm" title="Bro, Stockholm">Bro</a> near <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> Sörenstam's father Tom is a retired <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> executive and her mother Gunilla worked in a bank. Her younger sister <a href="/wiki/Charlotta_S%C3%B6renstam" title="Charlotta Sörenstam">Charlotta</a> is a professional golfer who coaches at her sister's academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LottaLPGA_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-LottaLPGA-5">[5]</a></sup> Annika and Charlotta Sörenstam are the only two sisters to have both won $1 million on the LPGA.</p>
<p>As a child, Sörenstam was a talented all-round sportsgirl. She was a nationally-ranked junior <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> player, played <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> (soccer) in her hometown team Bro IK, and was such a good <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing" title="Alpine skiing">skier</a> that the coach of the Swedish national ski team suggested the family move to northern Sweden to improve her skiing year round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Red_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Red-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_golf">Junior golf</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Junior golf">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the age of 12, she switched to golf, sharing her first set of golf clubs with her sister—Annika got the odd numbered clubs and Charlotta the even—and earned her first handicap of 54.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> She was so shy as a junior she used to deliberately three-putt at the end of a tournament to avoid giving the victory speech.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACAD3_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACAD3-8">[8]</a></sup> The coaches noticed and at the next tournament both the winner and the runner-up had to give a speech. Sörenstam decided that if she were going to have to face the crowd anyway she might as well win and the deliberate misses stopped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swedish_national_team">Swedish national team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Swedish national team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Her successful amateur career included a win in the St. Rule Trophy played at <a href="/wiki/Old_Course_at_St_Andrews" title="Old Course at St Andrews">St. Andrews</a> and a runner-up finish in the Swedish national mother/daughter golf tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-St_Rule_Trophy_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-St_Rule_Trophy-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sis_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sis-10">[10]</a></sup> As a member of the Swedish National Team from 1987 to 1992, she played in the 1990 and 1992 <a href="/wiki/Espirito_Santo_Trophy" title="Espirito Santo Trophy">Espirito Santo Trophy</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Amateur_Golf_Team_Championships" title="World Amateur Golf Team Championships">World Amateur Golf Team Championships</a>, becoming World Amateur champion in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGF_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGF-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGF2_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGF2-12">[12]</a></sup> While waiting to start college in Sweden, Sörenstam worked as a personal assistant at the Swedish PGA and played on the Swedish Ladies Telia Tour, winning three tournaments during 1990/1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PGA_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-PGA-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tel1989_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tel1989-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tel1990_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tel1990-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tel1991_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tel1991-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Arizona">University of Arizona</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: University of Arizona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a coach spotted Sörenstam playing in a collegiate event in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, she moved to the U.S. to play college golf at the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats" title="Arizona Wildcats">University of Arizona</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> She won seven collegiate titles and in 1991, became the first non-American and first freshman to win the individual <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Women%27s_Golf_Championships" title="NCAA Division I Women's Golf Championships">NCAA Division I Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sis_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sis-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCAA_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA-17">[17]</a></sup> Sörenstam was 1991 NCAA Co-Player of the Year with <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Robbins" title="Kelly Robbins">Kelly Robbins</a>, runner-up in the 1992 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Women%27s_Golf_Championships" title="NCAA Division I Women's Golf Championships">NCAA championship</a>, 1992 <a href="/wiki/Pac-12_Conference" title="Pac-12 Conference">Pac-10</a> champion and a 1991–92 NCAA <a href="/wiki/All-America" title="All-America">All-American</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAC_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAC-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCAAAll_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCAAAll-19">[19]</a></sup> She qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1992_U.S._Women%27s_Open_Golf_Championship" title="1992 U.S. Women's Open Golf Championship">U.S. Women's Open</a> at <a href="/wiki/Oakmont_Country_Club" title="Oakmont Country Club">Oakmont</a> in July, made the cut, and tied for 63rd. A few weeks later at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Women%27s_Amateur" title="U.S. Women's Amateur">U.S. Women's Amateur</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kemper_Lakes_Golf_Club" title="Kemper Lakes Golf Club">Kemper Lakes</a> near <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, she was the runner-up to <a href="/wiki/Vicki_Goetze" title="Vicki Goetze">Vicki Goetze</a>, bogeying the last hole in the 36-hole final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAm_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAm-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAm_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAm-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtzewrga_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-gtzewrga-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erguswam92_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-erguswam92-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Professional career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sörenstam turned professional in 1992, but missed her LPGA Tour card at the final <a href="/wiki/Qualifying_school" title="Qualifying school">qualifying tournament</a> by one shot, and began her professional career on the <a href="/wiki/Ladies_European_Tour" title="Ladies European Tour">Ladies European Tour</a> (LET), formerly known as the WPGET.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> She was invited to play in three LPGA Tour events in <a href="/wiki/1993_LPGA_Tour" title="1993 LPGA Tour">1993</a>, where she finished T38th, 4th, and T9th, earning more than $47,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Bio_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010Bio-23">[23]</a></sup> She finished second four times on the <a href="/wiki/Ladies_European_Tour" title="Ladies European Tour">Ladies European Tour</a> and was 1993 <a href="/wiki/Ladies_European_Tour#Yearly_award_winners" title="Ladies European Tour">Ladies European Tour Rookie of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LETBio_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-LETBio-24">[24]</a></sup> By tying for 28th at the LPGA Final Qualifying Tournament she earned non-exempt status for the <a href="/wiki/1994_LPGA_Tour" title="1994 LPGA Tour">1994</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> Sörenstam's first professional win came at the 1994 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holden_Women%27s_Australian_Open" title="Holden Women's Australian Open">Holden Women's Australian Open</a> on the <a href="/wiki/ALPG_Tour" title="ALPG Tour">ALPG Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alpg1994_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-alpg1994-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, Sörenstam was <a href="/wiki/LPGA#LPGA_Tour_awards" title="LPGA">LPGA Rookie of the Year</a>, had three top-10 finishes including a tie for second at the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_British_Open" title="Women's British Open">Women's British Open</a> and made her <a href="/wiki/1994_Solheim_Cup" title="1994 Solheim Cup">Solheim Cup</a> debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LETBio_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-LETBio-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SolTeams_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-SolTeams-26">[26]</a></sup> Her breakout year was <a href="/wiki/1995_LPGA_Tour" title="1995 LPGA Tour">1995</a>, when she won her first LPGA Tour title at the <a href="/wiki/1995_U.S._Women%27s_Open_Golf_Championship" title="1995 U.S. Women's Open Golf Championship">U.S. Women's Open</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-8"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> She finished at the top of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour#Leading_money_winners_by_year" title="LPGA Tour">Money List</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Money_List_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Money_List-27">[27]</a></sup> and was the first non-American winner of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour#LPGA_Tour_awards" title="LPGA Tour">Vare Trophy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vare_Trophy_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vare_Trophy-28">[28]</a></sup> She became the second player ever to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour#LPGA_Tour_awards" title="LPGA Tour">Player of the Year</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour#LPGA_Tour_awards" title="LPGA Tour">Vare Trophy</a> winner the year after being Rookie of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LPGABio_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-LPGABio-29">[29]</a></sup> A win at the 1995 Australian Ladies Masters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1995alpgt_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-1995alpgt-30">[30]</a></sup> and two other wins on the Ladies European Tour put her top of the <a href="/wiki/Ladies_European_Tour#Yearly_award_winners" title="Ladies European Tour">LET Order of Merit</a> and made her the first player to top both the European and LPGA Tour money lists in the same season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LETBio_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-LETBio-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5Tours_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-5Tours-31">[31]</a></sup> Her success worldwide resulted in her winning the <a href="/wiki/Radiosportens_Jerringpris" title="Radiosportens Jerringpris">Jerringpriset</a> award in Sweden,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerring1995_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jerring1995-32">[32]</a></sup> the country's most prestigious award in sports as well as being awarded the <a href="/wiki/Svenska_Dagbladet_Gold_Medal" title="Svenska Dagbladet Gold Medal">Svenska Dagbladet Gold Medal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SvenDag_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-SvenDag-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>1996 saw Sörenstam win her home LET tournament, the Trygg Hansa Ladies' Open in Sweden and three LPGA tournaments including the U.S. Women's Open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trygg_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trygg-34">[34]</a></sup> In defending her title, she became the first non-American to win back to back U.S. Women's Open titles,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> passed the $1 million mark in LPGA career earnings, and won her second consecutive Vare Trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Bio_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-2010Bio-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>She won six tour events in <a href="/wiki/1997_LPGA_Tour" title="1997 LPGA Tour">1997</a>, regaining the money list and player of the year titles. Internationally, she won on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JLPGA" title="JLPGA">JLPGA</a> and defended her home LET title at the renamed Compaq Open. She became the first player in LPGA history to finish a season with a sub-70 scoring average of 69.99 en route to retaining the 1998 Player of the Year and Money List titles as well as winning the LET Swedish tour stop for the third time running.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vare_Trophy_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vare_Trophy-28">[28]</a></sup> September 1999 saw Sörenstam change her on-course team replacing her caddie of six years, Colin Cann, with Terry McNamara.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cann_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cann-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMac_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMac-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At this point in her career, Sörenstam says she lost focus having reached her biggest goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Annika.27s_Way_4-10"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Annika.27s_Way-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karrie_Webb" title="Karrie Webb">Karrie Webb</a> became the best LPGA Tour player but Sörenstam still managed to win more LPGA tournaments than any other LPGA Tour player during the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LPGABio_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-LPGABio-29">[29]</a></sup> She qualified for the <a href="/wiki/World_Golf_Hall_of_Fame" title="World Golf Hall of Fame">World Golf Hall of Fame</a> when she won the <a href="/wiki/2000_LPGA_Tour" title="2000 LPGA Tour">2000</a> <a href="/wiki/Welch%27s/Fry%27s_Championship" title="Welch's/Fry's Championship">Welch's/Circle K Championship</a>, but was not eligible for induction until finishing her tenth year on the LPGA tour in October 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOF1_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-HOF1-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOF2_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-HOF2-38">[38]</a></sup> Sörenstam was the first international player to be inducted into the Hall of Fame through the LPGA criteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOF3_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-HOF3-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSF_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSF-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOF4_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-HOF4-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Having lost her preeminent position, Sörenstam embarked on a new five-day-a-week exercise program including weight-lifting and balance work which by 2003 added over 20 yards (18 m) to her driving distance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Passion_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Passion-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Driving_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Driving-43">[43]</a></sup> During the 2001 season, she had eight LPGA wins, became the only female golfer to shoot a 59 in competition and the first LPGA player to cross the $2 million mark in single-season earnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Money_List_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Money_List-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Score59_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Score59-44">[44]</a></sup> She set or tied a total of 30 LPGA records en route to regaining the Vare Trophy and winning her fourth Player of the Year and Money List titles in 2001. In a made-for-TV alternate shot competition between the two best male and female players in the world, Sörenstam and <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Woods" title="Tiger Woods">Tiger Woods</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Karrie_Webb" title="Karrie Webb">Karrie Webb</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Duval" title="David Duval">David Duval</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bighorn_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bighorn-45">[45]</a></sup></p>

</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of that season <a href="/wiki/Karrie_Webb" title="Karrie Webb">Karrie Webb</a> said she "would eat her hat" if Sörenstam repeated her eight wins in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WebbHat_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-WebbHat-46">[46]</a></sup> Sörenstam accomplished that feat, joining <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Wright" title="Mickey Wright">Mickey Wright</a> as the only players to win 11 LPGA tournaments in one season, earning her fifth Player of the Year title and fifth Vare Trophy. She successfully defended the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kraft_Nabisco_Championship" title="Kraft Nabisco Championship">Kraft Nabisco Championship</a>, her fourth major victory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KNC2002_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-KNC2002-47">[47]</a></sup> and also won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ANZ_Ladies_Masters" title="ANZ Ladies Masters">ANZ Ladies Masters</a> in Australia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANZ2002_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANZ2002-48">[48]</a></sup> and Compaq Open in Sweden on the <a href="/wiki/Ladies_European_Tour" title="Ladies European Tour">Ladies European Tour</a> giving her 13 wins in 25 starts worldwide in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Compaq2002_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Compaq2002-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amid notable controversy, Sörenstam was invited to play in the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Colonial" title="Bank of America Colonial">Bank of America Colonial</a> golf tournament in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, in May <a href="/wiki/2003_PGA_Tour" title="2003 PGA Tour">2003</a>, making her the first woman to play in a PGA Tour event since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babe_Zaharias" title="Babe Zaharias">Babe Zaharias</a>, who qualified for the 1945 <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Open" title="Los Angeles Open">Los Angeles Open</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vijay_Singh" title="Vijay Singh">Vijay Singh</a>, fourth in the world rankings at the time, was particularly critical of her presence; he was quoted saying she had no business playing and he hoped she missed the cut, although this statement was later proven to be misquoted and he later apologized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vijay_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vijay-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vijay2_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vijay2-52">[52]</a></sup> Cheered through each hole, she shot five over par, tying for 96th out of the 111 who finished the first two rounds, missing the cut. After shooting 1-over-par 71 in the first round, finishing in 73rd and on pace to challenge for a weekend spot, Sörenstam said she was nervous all day but pleased by her performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colonialpost_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-colonialpost-53">[53]</a></sup> Through the first round she led the field in driving accuracy, was in the top 20 in greens in regulation, and was 84th out of 111 in driving distance. Unfortunately, poor putting (last in the field, averaging over a two-putt) cost her a spot on the first page of the first round leaderboard and ultimately caused her to miss the cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later in the 2003 season, she won the LPGA Championship and the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_British_Open" title="Women's British Open">Women's British Open</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brit2003_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brit2003-55">[55]</a></sup> becoming only the sixth player to complete the LPGA Career Grand Slam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Career_Slam_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Career_Slam-56">[56]</a></sup> She had five other victories worldwide, set or tied a total of 22 LPGA records and earned her sixth Player of the Year award. She competed against <a href="/wiki/Fred_Couples" title="Fred Couples">Fred Couples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Mickelson" title="Phil Mickelson">Phil Mickelson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_O%27Meara" title="Mark O'Meara">Mark O'Meara</a> in the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Skins_Game_(PGA_Tour)" title="Skins Game (PGA Tour)">Skins Game</a>, finishing second with five skins worth $225,000; Sörenstam holed a 39-yard (36 m) bunker shot on the ninth hole—the eighth eagle in Skins Game history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skins_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Skins-57">[57]</a></sup> In September, she was part of the winning European <a href="/wiki/2003_Solheim_Cup" title="2003 Solheim Cup">Solheim Cup</a> team in her native Sweden. She was awarded her second Jerringpriset award in Sweden<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerring2003_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jerring2003-58">[58]</a></sup> plus the 2003 Golf Writers' Trophy by the Association of Golf Writers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GWT_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-GWT-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sörenstam's dominance continued in 2004 with her seventh LPGA Player of the Year award tying <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Whitworth" title="Kathy Whitworth">Kathy Whitworth</a> for the most in LPGA history. She posted 16 top-10 finishes in 18 LPGA starts, including eight wins, had two additional international wins, became the first player to reach $15 million in LPGA career earnings and took her own LPGA single-season scoring average record to 68.69696, but played too few rounds to win the Vare Trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LPGA_Records_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-LPGA_Records-60">[60]</a></sup> The Women's Sports Foundation gave her the 2004 Sportswoman of the Year Award,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSF_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSF-40">[40]</a></sup> and the Laureus World Sports Academy named her <a href="/wiki/Laureus_World_Sports_Award_for_Sportswoman_of_the_Year" title="Laureus World Sports Award for Sportswoman of the Year">World Sportswoman of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laureus_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Laureus-61">[61]</a></sup> She also released a combination autobiography and golf instructional book, <i>Golf Annika's Way</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Book_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Book-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sörenstam's life both on and off the golf course changed in <a href="/wiki/2005_LPGA_Tour" title="2005 LPGA Tour">2005</a>. In February, she announced that she had filed for divorce from David Esch, her husband of eight years, and this was finalised in August but it did not adversely affect her golf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Divorce_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Divorce-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DivFinal_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-DivFinal-64">[64]</a></sup> Her achievements included being the first player in LPGA history to win a major three consecutive years at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Championship" title="LPGA Championship">LPGA Championship</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McD2_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-McD2-65">[65]</a></sup> and the first golfer in LPGA or PGA history to win the same event five consecutive years at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mizuno_Classic" title="Mizuno Classic">Mizuno Classic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mizuno_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mizuno-66">[66]</a></sup> 11 wins in 21 tournaments entered worldwide included victory in the Scandinavian TPC hosted by Annika<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPC1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-TPC1-67">[67]</a></sup> where she presented <i>herself</i> the trophy, giving her an eighth Money List title, tying the LPGA record, an eighth Rolex Player of the Year (POY) award (a record) and a sixth Vare Trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vare_Trophy_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vare_Trophy-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POY_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-POY-68">[68]</a></sup> She is the only LPGA player ever to win Money List, POY award and Vare trophy in the same year in five different years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Syba_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Syba-69">[69]</a></sup> Team competition saw her make her seventh consecutive Solheim Cup appearance, her 4 points making her total 21, the event's all-time leading points earner,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solheim_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Solheim-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005Sol_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-2005Sol-71">[71]</a></sup> and the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Lexus_Cup" title="Lexus Cup">Lexus Cup</a> was played with Sörenstam as the Captain of the victorious International Team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lexus1_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lexus1-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="1534" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG/220px-SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG/330px-SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG/440px-SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SorenstamBrit2004c.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sörenstam at the Women's British Open 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>These events resulted in her receiving numerous awards. The Golf Writers Association of America named Sörenstam Female Player of the Year for the eighth time (1995,1997, 2000–2005),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gwaa1_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gwaa1-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gwaa2_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gwaa2-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gwaa3_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gwaa3-75">[75]</a></sup> Associated Press voted her <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press_Athlete_of_the_Year" title="Associated Press Athlete of the Year">Female Athlete of the Year</a> for the third consecutive year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP1_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP1-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP2_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP2-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP3_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP3-78">[78]</a></sup> and she became the first woman to win the Golf Writers' Trophy twice in the 55-year history of European golf's most prestigious award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GWT2_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-GWT2-79">[79]</a></sup> Having previously won six <a href="/wiki/Best_Female_Golfer_ESPY_Award" title="Best Female Golfer ESPY Award">Best Female Golfer ESPY Awards</a> (1996, 1998–99, 2002–04), Sörenstam also received the 2005 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPY_Awards" title="ESPY Awards">ESPY Award</a> as <a href="/wiki/Best_Female_Athlete_ESPY_Award" title="Best Female Athlete ESPY Award">Best Female Athlete</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espy1_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-espy1-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espy2_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-espy2-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espy3_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-espy3-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espy4_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-espy4-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the first-ever official <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_World_Golf_Rankings" title="Women's World Golf Rankings">Women's World Golf Rankings</a> were unveiled in February <a href="/wiki/2006_LPGA_Tour" title="2006 LPGA Tour">2006</a>, Sörenstam was confirmed as the number-one player in women's golf, a position she relinquished to <a href="/wiki/Lorena_Ochoa" title="Lorena Ochoa">Lorena Ochoa</a> on 22 April <a href="/wiki/2007_LPGA_Tour" title="2007 LPGA Tour">2007</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CareerMoney_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-CareerMoney-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolex_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolex-85">[85]</a></sup> In partnership with <a href="/wiki/Liselotte_Neumann" title="Liselotte Neumann">Liselotte Neumann</a> in team Sweden, she won the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_World_Cup_of_Golf" title="Women's World Cup of Golf">Women's World Cup of Golf</a>, opened her LPGA season with a defence of her title in the <a href="/wiki/MasterCard_Classic" title="MasterCard Classic">MasterCard Classic</a>. She then went winless in eight starts, causing some to talk of a slump.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWCG_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWCG-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slump_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slump-87">[87]</a></sup> Her winning drought ended at the <a href="/wiki/2006_U.S._Women%27s_Open_Golf_Championship" title="2006 U.S. Women's Open Golf Championship">U.S. Women's Open</a>, where she won an 18-hole playoff over Pat Hurst for her tenth major championship title, tying her for third on the list of players with most major championship titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LPGA_Wins_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-LPGA_Wins-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-US-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> She totalled 3 wins on the LPGA and two on the Ladies European Tour, the inaugural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dubai_Ladies_Masters" title="Dubai Ladies Masters">Dubai Ladies Masters</a> and the Swedish tournament she hosts, which she defended in her home town at the course where she learned to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dubai_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dubai-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPC2_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-TPC2-91">[91]</a></sup> Her International team lost the second Lexus Cup competition to Team Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lexus2_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lexus2-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sörenstam started 2007 by losing a playoff while defending of her MasterCard Classic title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007Mex_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-2007Mex-93">[93]</a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kraft_Nabisco_Championship" title="Kraft Nabisco Championship">Kraft Nabisco Championship</a> she shot her highest 72-hole score in a major in nine years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nab2007_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nab2007-94">[94]</a></sup> a result explained by her subsequent diagnosis with ruptured and bulging discs in her neck, the first major injury in Sörenstam's 13-year LPGA career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disclpga_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disclpga-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiscESPN_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiscESPN-96">[96]</a></sup> After a two-month injury rehabilitation break, Sörenstam returned as the Ginn Tribute tournament hostess where she admitted to being at only 85% fitness and finished tied for 36th place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GinnTrib_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-GinnTrib-97">[97]</a></sup> She was still not fully fit in her next two tournaments, the LPGA Championship where she finished tied for 15th place, and the US Women's Open, where, as defending champion, she finished tied for 32nd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USOpen07_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-USOpen07-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annika18thTee.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="788" data-file-width="644" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Annika18thTee.JPG/220px-Annika18thTee.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Annika18thTee.JPG/330px-Annika18thTee.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Annika18thTee.JPG/440px-Annika18thTee.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annika18thTee.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sörenstam at the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_British_Open" title="Women's British Open">Women's British Open</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007_Women%27s_British_Open" title="2007 Women's British Open">2007</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After an early round defeat at the World Matchplay Championship, Sörenstam finished sixth at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evian_Masters" title="Evian Masters">Evian Masters</a>, 16th at the Women's British Open and ninth in the Swedish tournament she hosts on the Ladies European Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU2_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU2-99">[99]</a></sup> On her return to the US, Sörenstam had three top ten finishes but missed the weekend at the season closing ADT Playoffs for the second year running. However, Sörenstam did win a worldwide title at the Dubai Ladies Masters on the Ladies European Tour in November 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADT08_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADT08-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dubai2_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dubai2-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Declaring herself recovered from injury and ready to return to a complete season of competitive golf in 2008, Sörenstam opened the year at the <a href="/wiki/SBS_Open_at_Turtle_Bay" title="SBS Open at Turtle Bay">SBS Open at Turtle Bay</a> where she captured her 70th LPGA Tour victory and first since September 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sbs08_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-sbs08-102">[102]</a></sup> She won next at the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_International_Pro-Am" title="Stanford International Pro-Am">Stanford International Pro-Am</a> in April then following a week off, won again at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michelob_ULTRA_Open_at_Kingsmill" title="Michelob ULTRA Open at Kingsmill">Michelob ULTRA Open at Kingsmill</a> in a tournament record score, giving her three wins and over $1 million in earnings by mid-May. It was her 72nd and final ever win on the LPGA Tour.</p>
<p>In 2008, Sörenstam was highly critical of other female golfers who tried to play in the PGA Tour – her comments to <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Wie" title="Michelle Wie">Michelle Wie</a> for playing on the men's tour: "I really don't know why Michelle continues to do this. We have a major this week and, if you can't qualify for a major, I don't see any reason why you should play with the men."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Awie_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Awie-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 May 2008, Sörenstam announced at a press conference at the Sybase Classic that she would "step away" from competitive golf at the conclusion of the 2008 season. That night, she threw out the first pitch of the Washington Nationals/New York Mets baseball game at Shea Stadium in New York and the following day read the Top Ten on the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retirement_lpga_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-retirement_lpga-104">[104]</a></sup> Her last tournament victory came in a playoff at the Suzhou Taihu Ladies Open, an event co-sanctioned by the Ladies European Tour and the Ladies Asian Golf tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-China-105">[105]</a></sup> Her last scheduled tournament on the LPGA Tour was the season-ending <a href="/wiki/ADT_Championship" title="ADT Championship">ADT Championship</a> in November, where she failed to make the weekend play in the event's unique playoff structure. Her final sanctioned LPGA appearance was as the winning captain of Team International at the 2008 Lexus Cup in Singapore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lex2008_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lex2008-106">[106]</a></sup> Her last professional tournament was the Dubai Ladies Masters on the Ladies European Tour in December 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retirement_gc_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-retirement_gc-107">[107]</a></sup> where she finished tied for 7th.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_career">Business career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Business career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Sörenstam began the transition from professional golfer to entrepreneur during the later years of her career, attempting to combine golf, fitness and charitable works into various businesses under the ANNIKA brand with the brand statement "Share my Passion". They are all promoted by her website on which there is a blog to which she and her staff regularly contribute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Passion2_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Passion2-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Website_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Website-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blog_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blog-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beau_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beau-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Golf_course_design">Golf course design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Golf course design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sörenstam has undertaken a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golf_course_design" title="Golf course design">golf course design</a> projects. Her first, the Annika Course, was completed at <a href="/wiki/Mission_Hills_Golf_Club" title="Mission Hills Golf Club">Mission Hills Golf Club</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzen" title="Shenzen">Shenzen</a>, China, in 2003; the second was officially launched in January 2006 and opened in 2008 at Euphoria Golf Estate &amp; Hydro in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mission1_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mission1-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACourse1_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-SACourse1-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACourse2_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-SACourse2-114">[114]</a></sup> She recently announced a new project at Mines Golf City, near <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia. Projects closer to home include a redesign of the Patriots Point Links Course near <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston, South Carolina</a> and a course at <a href="/wiki/Red_Mountain_Resort" title="Red Mountain Resort">Red Mountain Resort</a>, British Columbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Red_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Red-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patriot_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Patriot-115">[115]</a></sup> She and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Nicklaus" title="Jack Nicklaus">Jack Nicklaus</a> lost out on their bid to build the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_golf_course" title="Olympic golf course">Olympic golf course</a> in Rio to <a href="/wiki/Gil_Hanse" title="Gil Hanse">Gil Hanse</a> and his consultant <a href="/wiki/Amy_Alcott" title="Amy Alcott">Amy Alcott</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RioGolf_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-RioGolf-116">[116]</a></sup> In 2010, a golf course at Golden Bay Resort was opened in South Korea. She designed this golf course, and Hanhwa Hotels &amp; Resorts Corporation developed. This was the first project for her after-retirement golf course design.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_ANNIKA_Academy">The ANNIKA Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The ANNIKA Academy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ANNIKA Academy at Ginn Reunion Resort in <a href="/wiki/Reunion,_Florida" title="Reunion, Florida">Reunion, Florida</a> began construction in 2006 and opened in April 2007 with Sörenstam's longtime coach Henri Reis serving as head instructor, her sister Charlotta an instructor and club fitter, her personal trainer Kai Fusser focusing on overall fitness training, and with Sorenstam available for coaching on certain golfing packages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACAD3_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-ACAD3-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Academy_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Academy-117">[117]</a></sup> The opening ceremony included a <a href="/wiki/Make-A-Wish_Foundation" title="Make-A-Wish Foundation">Make-A-Wish Foundation</a> golf clinic conducted by Sörenstam who is a United States ambassador for the Make-A-Wish Foundation and it also hosted clinics for junior golfers during The Annika Invitational, an <a href="/wiki/American_Junior_Golf_Association" title="American Junior Golf Association">American Junior Golf Association</a> invitation-only event featuring the top 60 girls from around the world hosted by The ANNIKA Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wish_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wish-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajga1_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ajga1-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajga2_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ajga2-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_business_ventures">Other business ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other business ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other branches of the ANNIKA business include a clothing line with <a href="/wiki/Cutter_%26_Buck" title="Cutter &amp; Buck">Cutter &amp; Buck</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cutter-renew_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-cutter-renew-121">[121]</a></sup> a limited label wine produced in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Wente_Vineyards" title="Wente Vineyards">Wente Vineyards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wine-announce_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-wine-announce-122">[122]</a></sup> and a signature fragrance developed by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SA_Fragrances&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SA Fragrances (page does not exist)">SA Fragrances</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fragrance-announce_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-fragrance-announce-123">[123]</a></sup> Sörenstam also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Ginn_Tribute_Hosted_by_Annika" title="Ginn Tribute Hosted by Annika">Ginn Tribute Hosted by Annika</a>, an event on the LPGA Tour in 2007 and 2008, and the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_TPC_hosted_by_Annika" title="Scandinavian TPC hosted by Annika">Scandinavian TPC hosted by Annika</a> on the Ladies European Tour during its last four years from 2005 through 2008. She won the latter tournament in 2005 and 2006. Both tournaments had their last event in 2008.</p>
<p>One of Sörenstam's hobbies is cooking. She has participated in cooking demonstrations during LPGA tournaments and has talked about enrolling in cooking school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WegCook_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-WegCook-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChefMing_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChefMing-125">[125]</a></sup> Before the 2003 season Sörenstam took the opportunity to improve her culinary skills by working eight-hour shifts in the kitchens of the Lake Nona Country Club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chef_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chef-126">[126]</a></sup> Sörenstam has had a serious interest in investments, real estate and the stock market since she earned her first LPGA check and in August 2006 was invited to ring the closing bell at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Int_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Int-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSE1_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYSE1-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASBrit2005a.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/ASBrit2005a.JPG/220px-ASBrit2005a.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/ASBrit2005a.JPG/330px-ASBrit2005a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/ASBrit2005a.JPG/440px-ASBrit2005a.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ASBrit2005a.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sörenstam at the Women's British Open 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sörenstam has been described as an atheist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> She met her first husband David Esch in 1994 on the driving range at Moon Valley Country Club, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, where she was an LPGA rookie practicing for a tournament and he worked for club manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Ping_(golf)" title="Ping (golf)">Ping</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Esch1_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Esch1-130">[130]</a></sup> They were engaged at the 1995 Evian Masters, married in Lake Tahoe on 4 January 1997, and were divorced in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Divorce_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Divorce-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conv_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conv-131">[131]</a></sup> In August 2007 she married Mike McGee, the managing director for the ANNIKA brand of businesses and son of former PGA Tour and Champions Tour player <a href="/wiki/Jerry_McGee" title="Jerry McGee">Jerry McGee</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nona_Golf_%26_Country_Club" title="Lake Nona Golf &amp; Country Club">Lake Nona Golf &amp; Country Club</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>, on 10 January 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retirement_gc_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-retirement_gc-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mar_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mar-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mar2_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mar2-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their daughter Ava Madelyn McGee was born 1 September 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pregnant_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-pregnant-135">[135]</a></sup> On 21 March 2011, Sörenstam gave birth to a son, William Nicholas McGee, nine weeks premature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Babyno2_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Babyno2-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golf_Digest_3-2011_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Golf_Digest_3-2011-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_wins_.2893.29">Professional wins (93)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Professional wins (93)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_ranking">World ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: World ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Position in <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_World_Golf_Rankings" title="Women's World Golf Rankings">Women's World Golf Rankings</a> at the end of each calendar year.</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; font-size: 95%;">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Ranking</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2006</td>
<td>1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2007</td>
<td>4<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2008</td>
<td>3<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><small>On 12 January 2009, Sörenstam, who was ranked third the previous week despite having announced her retirement effective at the end of the 2008 season, was removed from the rankings. No official explanation was given for her removal. Sörenstam later posted in her personal blog that she asked to be removed.</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolex-removal_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-rolex-removal-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_appearances">Team appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Annika_S%C3%B6renstam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Team appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</ul>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Solheim_Cup" title="Solheim Cup">Solheim Cup</a> (representing Europe): <a href="/wiki/1994_Solheim_Cup" title="1994 Solheim Cup">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/1996_Solheim_Cup" title="1996 Solheim Cup">1996</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998_Solheim_Cup" title="1998 Solheim Cup">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000_Solheim_Cup" title="2000 Solheim Cup">2000</a> (winners), <a href="/wiki/2002_Solheim_Cup" title="2002 Solheim Cup">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_Solheim_Cup" title="2003 Solheim Cup">2003</a> (winners), <a href="/wiki/2005_Solheim_Cup" title="2005 Solheim Cup">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Solheim_Cup" title="2007 Solheim Cup">2007</a></li>
